<div id="review_783440554" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/783440554" />
    <a title="Loopy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3221360-loopy"><img alt="Loopy" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/783440554?book_show_action=true">Dec 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Loopy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Loopy" href="/user/show/3221360-loopy">Loopy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3221360-loopy?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3221360-loopy?shelf=series">series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer783440554" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10986207477139528781">Orson Scott Card - you may think that unless you have babies your life is meaningless (in fact you must think that, as so many of your characters gives us at least one lecture on it at one point or another in this novel) but guess what? I don't think that, and there are plenty of other people like me out there that don't think it either. The only thing that continually trying to ram this fallacy down my throat does is make me wonder whether a. you've been brainwashed b. you're not convinced but </span>
  <span id="freeText10986207477139528781" style="display:none">Orson Scott Card - you may think that unless you have babies your life is meaningless (in fact you must think that, as so many of your characters gives us at least one lecture on it at one point or another in this novel) but guess what? I don't think that, and there are plenty of other people like me out there that don't think it either. The only thing that continually trying to ram this fallacy down my throat does is make me wonder whether a. you've been brainwashed b. you're not convinced but you're still trying to convince yourself c. you know it's not true but you want everyone else to make the same mistake you feel you made d. you're an utter twat. This constant preaching without enough interesting plot to carry it is really turning me off. What you did to Anton? Completely revolting.<br /><br />Surely I'm not the only one that is wondering if Bean is actually old enough to produce viable sperm? His whole romance with Petra ....... it feels a bit like paedophilia. Isn't he only about 10? Oh, another thing, please, please, please either leave any hint of romance out or get someone else to write it - it's excruciating to read and I want to gag whenever Ender's parents converse with each other.<br /><br />Seems incongruous that Bean and Petra chose <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Barcelona's most famous cathedral to get married in when they were trying to keep such a low profile. And that whole fiasco at the hospital? Yes, I can see why you'd hire some random security guard for what you see as so important, rather than use some of the elite force you'd trained yourself  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> - makes complete sense ...... if you're a complete fool.<br /><br />Oh, another thing. It was hard enough for me to believe the whole Virlomi diety story line before - maybe because I'm more inclined to look for a rational explanation rather than jump to a supernatural one and expect others to do the same. Yes, I can see some lost tribe without any access to the modern world believing the supernatural first due to their lack of familiarity with technology. I find it hard to believe that there are large groups of Indian military ready to believe a supernatural being is behind something that is easily explained in the present time, let alone well into the future. <br /><br />I'm sure I could come up with more things that annoyed me but I'll leave it there .......... and yes, I'll keep reading - I'm curious to see what happens and I'm kind of looking forward to Petra and Ender's mother kicking the bucket.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10986207477139528781" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('4iyES+fEZlT7dEPSzH9hGBM3RIXItthOG5QmtXe0MMziO+7NbB2chi3QHfuCyt5pzw3hQt0cU0frNYJQNgqSxw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer17982675340426218133">Orson Scott Card is the author of the novels <i>Ender's Game</i>, <i>Ender's Shadow</i>, and <i>Speaker for the Dead</i>, which are widely read by adults and younger readers, and are increasingly used in schools.<br/><br/>Besides these and other science fiction novels, Card writes contemporary fantasy (<i>Magic Street</i>, <i>Enchantment</i>, <i>Lost Boys</i>), biblical novels (<i>Stone Tables</i>, <i>Rachel and Leah</i>), the American frontier fantasy series Th</span>
  <span id="freeText17982675340426218133" style="display:none">Orson Scott Card is the author of the novels <i>Ender's Game</i>, <i>Ender's Shadow</i>, and <i>Speaker for the Dead</i>, which are widely read by adults and younger readers, and are increasingly used in schools.<br /><br />Besides these and other science fiction novels, Card writes contemporary fantasy (<i>Magic Street</i>, <i>Enchantment</i>, <i>Lost Boys</i>), biblical novels (<i>Stone Tables</i>, <i>Rachel and Leah</i>), the American frontier fantasy series The Tales of Alvin Maker (beginning with <i>Seventh Son</i>), poetry (<i>An Open Book</i>), and many plays and scripts.<br /><br />Card was born in Washington and grew up in California, Arizona, and Utah. He served a mission for the LDS Church in Brazil in the early 1970s. Besides his writing, he teaches occasional classes and workshops and directs plays. He recently began a long-term position as a professor of writing and literature at Southern Virginia University.<br /><br />Card currently lives in Greensboro, North Carolina, with his wife, Kristine Allen Card, and their youngest child, Zina Margaret.<br /><br /><i>For further details, see the author's <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orson_Scott_Card" rel="nofollow noopener">Wikipedia</a> page.<br />For an ordered list of the author's works, see Wikipedia's <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_works_by_Orson_Scott_Card" rel="nofollow noopener">List of works by Orson Scott Card</a>.</i><br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://us.macmillan.com/author/orsonscottcard">http://us.macmillan.com/author/orsons...</a></span>
